name="articleBody"><div class="css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn"><div class="css-53u6y8"><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">WASHINGTON — At the end of August, when two top intelligence officials asked a Justice Department lawyer whether a whistle-blower’s complaint should be forwarded to Congress, they were told no, Attorney General William P. Barr and his department could handle the criminal referral against the president of the United States.</p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">About four weeks later, the department rendered its judgment: President Trump had not violated campaign finance laws when he <a class="css-1g7m0tk" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2019/09/25/us/politics/ukraine-transcript-trump.html?module=inline" title="">urged Ukraine’s president to work with Mr. Barr</a> to investigate a political rival, former Vice President Joseph R. Biden Jr.</p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">The very same evidence, a reconstructed transcript of a July call between Mr. Trump and Volodymyr Zelensky, has <a class="css-1g7m0tk" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2019/09/24/us/politics/democrats-impeachment-trump.html?module=inline" title="">whipped Washington into an impeachment crisis</a> in a matter of days.</p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">The sharply different responses to the call’s reconstruction, <a class="css-1g7m0tk" href="https://www.nytimes.com/interactive/2019/09/25/us/politics/trump-ukraine-transcript.html?action=click&amp;module=inline&amp;pgtype=Homepage" title="">released by the White House on Wednesday</a>, has helped further the perception that Mr. Trump regards Mr. Barr not as the nation’s highest law enforcement officer but as his political ally and legal protector.</p></div><aside class="css-o6xoe7"></aside></div><div class="css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn"><div class="css-53u6y8"><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">After congressional intelligence committees examined the full whistle-blower complaint on Wednesday afternoon, the House Intelligence Committee chairman, Representative Adam B. Schiff of California, said, “The idea that the Department of Justice would have intervened to prevent it from getting to Congress throws the leadership of the department into further ill repute.”</p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">Mr. Trump has long said that <a class="css-1g7m0tk" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2018/01/04/us/politics/trump-sessions-russia-mcgahn.html?module=inline" title="">the attorney general should shield him</a>, the way he believed Robert F. Kennedy protected his brother President John F. Kennedy, and Eric H. Holder Jr. protected President Barack Obama. He has told White House aides that he wants an attorney general who would be his Roy Cohn, referring to his onetime personal lawyer and fixer who once did the bidding of Senator Joseph R. McCarthy.</p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">The rough transcript showed that Mr. Trump believes he has that man. In a single sentence during the call with Ukraine’s leader, Mr. Trump said that he would have Rudolph W. Giuliani, his personal lawyer, and Mr. Barr reach out to help further an investigation of Mr. Biden and his younger son, Hunter Biden, who had served on the board of a Ukrainian corporation.</p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">“I will have Mr. Giuliani give you a call, and I am also going to have Attorney General Barr call, and we will get to the bottom of it,” Mr. Trump said.</p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">A Justice Department official said that Mr. Barr had no knowledge of the call until the director of national intelligence and the intelligence community’s inspector general sent the department the whistle-blower’s criminal referral late last month, and that Mr. Trump has not spoken with the attorney general “about having Ukraine investigate anything relating to former Vice President Biden or his son.”</p></div><aside class="css-o6xoe7"></aside></div><div class="css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn"><div class="css-53u6y8"><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">Mr. Trump has not asked Mr. Barr to contact Ukraine for any reason, Mr. Barr has not communicated with Ukraine on any topic, and Mr. Barr has not spoken with Mr. Giuliani about the president’s phone call “or anything relating to Ukraine,” a Justice Department spokeswoman, Kerri Kupec, said in a statement.</p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">But the department’s involvement in the case has been overwhelmingly positive for Mr. Trump. Not only did the department advise the acting director of national intelligence, Joseph Maguire, to keep the whistle-blower complaint from Congress, it unequivocally ruled out the possibility of criminal conduct on the part of the president.</p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">That outcome was in keeping with other determinations that have come out of the Justice Department regarding Mr. Trump. Time and again, department lawyers have said the president had not engaged in criminal or unethical behavior, whether it was potentially obstructing the investigation of the special counsel, Robert S. Mueller III, or criminally conspiring with Moscow as Russian intelligence agents tried to sway the 2016 election to Mr. Trump.</p></div><aside class="css-o6xoe7"></aside></div><div class="css-79elbk" data-testid="photoviewer-wrapper"><div class="css-z3e15g" data-testid="photoviewer-wrapper-hidden"></div><div class="css-1a48zt4 ehw59r15" data-testid="photoviewer-children"><figure aria-label="media" class="css-jcw7oy e1g7ppur0" itemid="https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/09/25/us/politics/25dc-justice2/merlin_161468916_de7fc191-5940-4277-905d-31ef45ec0337-articleLarge.jpg?quality=90&amp;auto=webp" itemprop="associatedMedia" itemscope="" itemtype="http://schema.org/ImageObject" role="group"><div class="css-1xdhyk6 erfvjey0"><span class="css-1ly73wi e1tej78p0">Image</span><img alt="Volodymyr Zelensky, the president of Ukraine, speaking Wednesday at the United Nations General Assembly. Mr. Trump told Mr. Zelensky that Mr. Barr could help him with investigations." class="css-1m50asq" itemid="https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/09/25/us/politics/25dc-justice2/merlin_161468916_de7fc191-5940-4277-905d-31ef45ec0337-articleLarge.jpg?quality=75&amp;auto=webp&amp;disable=upscale" itemprop="url" sizes="((min-width: 600px) and (max-width: 1004px)) 84vw, (min-width: 1005px) 60vw, 100vw" src="https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/09/25/us/politics/25dc-justice2/merlin_161468916_de7fc191-5940-4277-905d-31ef45ec0337-articleLarge.jpg?quality=75&amp;auto=webp&amp;disable=upscale" srcset="https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/09/25/us/politics/25dc-justice2/merlin_161468916_de7fc191-5940-4277-905d-31ef45ec0337-articleLarge.jpg?quality=90&amp;auto=webp 600w,https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/09/25/us/politics/25dc-justice2/merlin_161468916_de7fc191-5940-4277-905d-31ef45ec0337-jumbo.jpg?quality=90&amp;auto=webp 1024w,https://static01.nyt.com/images/2019/09/25/us/politics/25dc-justice2/merlin_161468916_de7fc191-5940-4277-905d-31ef45ec0337-superJumbo.jpg?quality=90&amp;auto=webp 2048w"/></div><figcaption class="css-1l44abu e1xdpqjp0" itemprop="caption description"><span aria-hidden="true" class="css-8i9d0s e13ogyst0">Volodymyr Zelensky, the president of Ukraine, speaking Wednesday at the United Nations General Assembly. Mr. Trump told Mr. Zelensky that Mr. Barr could help him with investigations.</span><span class="css-vuqh7u e1z0qqy90" itemprop="copyrightHolder"><span class="css-1ly73wi e1tej78p0">Credit</span><span>Brittainy Newman/The New York Times</span></span></figcaption></figure></div></div><div class="css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn"><div class="css-53u6y8"><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">Critics accused Mr. Barr of placing partisan politics over the rule of law when he released <a class="css-1g7m0tk" href="https://www.nytimes.com/interactive/2019/03/24/us/politics/barr-letter-mueller-report.html?module=inline" title="">what he said was a summary</a> of Mr. Mueller’s findings after a nearly two-year investigation of Russian election interference. Mr. Barr emphasized the special counsel’s determination that there was not enough evidence to show the Trump campaign had conspired with Russia, even though Mr. Mueller had said the campaign welcomed Russia’s help. And when Mr. Mueller declined to determine whether the president obstructed justice, Mr. Barr decided for him: He cleared Mr. Trump of the crime.</p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">Mr. Barr’s defenders say he is being judged unfairly. He was under no obligation to release Mr. Mueller’s report, which even in redacted form contained hundreds of pages of damning information about a person who was not charged with a crime.</p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">In the case of the Ukraine call, a criminal charge against the president was a far higher legal bar than the Constitution’s “high crimes and misdemeanors” bar for impeachment, which could mean pretty much whatever Congress wants it to mean.</p></div><aside class="css-o6xoe7"></aside></div><div class="css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn"><div class="css-53u6y8"><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">Since the <a class="css-1g7m0tk" href="https://www.nytimes.com/2019/04/18/us/politics/mueller-report-russian-interference-donald-trump.html?module=inline" title="">Mueller report was publicly released</a>, Mr. Barr has been involved in the day-to-day work of the department, traveling to United States attorneys’s offices, meeting with local law enforcement and taking part in issues of important to the White House like gun legislation and the carrying out of the president’s criminal justice reform law. He has also been intimately involved in the inquiry into the death of the accused sex trafficker Jeffrey Epstein.</p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">But Mr. Barr is also closely overseeing a review of the intelligence community’s decision to start a counterintelligence investigation into the Trump campaign during the 2016 election, which is being led by John Durham, the United States attorney in Connecticut. As part of that review, Mr. Durham is exploring what role, if any, a number of countries including Ukraine played in the investigation of the Trump campaign.</p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">“While the attorney general has yet to contact Ukraine in connection with this investigation, certain Ukrainians who are not members of the government have volunteered information to Mr. Durham, which he is evaluating,” Ms. Kupec said.</p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">In the case of the Ukraine call, the Justice Department’s Office of Legal Council determined early this month that the whistle-blower complaint should not be shared with Congress’s intelligence committees because it did not flag intelligence-related activities. Rather, it should be referred to the Justice Department as a possible violation of campaign finance law.</p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">Mr. Barr was not involved in the Justice Department’s review, which was overseen by the deputy attorney general, Jeffrey A. Rosen. It was led by the department’s criminal division and conducted by career prosecutors from the division’s public integrity section and the national security division.</p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">Last week, the criminal division concluded that there were no legal grounds for a criminal investigation in to Mr. Trump’s behavior.</p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">“All relevant components of the department agreed with this legal conclusion, and the department has concluded the matter,” Ms. Kupec said.</p></div><aside class="css-o6xoe7"></aside></div><div class="css-1fanzo5 StoryBodyCompanionColumn"><div class="css-53u6y8"><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">In coming to that conclusion, the Justice Department said the whistle-blower did not have firsthand knowledge of the call, and the intelligence community’s inspector general had said the whistle-blower could be politically biased. But senior department officials said their determination was based on the reconstructed transcript, not those other factors.</p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">They did not interview the participants on the call, which they are not obliged to do unless they open a criminal investigation. And they did not consider a Justice Department opinion that a sitting president cannot be indicted.</p><p class="css-exrw3m evys1bk0">“The Justice Department has not always taken the most aggressive reading of these kinds of campaign finance restrictions,” said Stephen I. Vladeck, a law professor at the University of Texas at Austin. “But that ought not cloud the obvious point that what the president did was wrong.”</p></div><aside class="css-2el0nj e16638kd0" datetime="2019-09-23T11:12:21-04:00">Sept. 23, 2019</time></div></div><div class="css-161i88g"><figure aria-label="media" class="" aria-labelledby="site-index-label" class="css-1ropbjl" data-testid="site-index" id="site-index"><div class="css-uw59u"><header class="css-jxzr5i" data-testid="site-index-header"><h2 class="css-vz7hjd" id="site-index-label">Site Index</h2><a href="/"><svg class="css-oylsik" fill="#000" viewbox="0 0 184 25" xmlns="http://www.w3.org/2000/svg"><path d="M13.8 2.9c0-2-1.9-2.5-3.4-2.5v.3c.9 0 1.6.3 1.6 1
